Women's Corner

The Misfortune of German Women 195

— Chen Yan

Chung Hwa Daily (Berlin Reuters Dispatch, February 18): "Today the authorities issued a red and black notice with the words 'Listed Criminals' written on it. Thus, the people of Xilin knew that the two female spies, namely the former Baroness Baek and Mrs. Nazina, were about to be executed. The two women were convicted of conspiring to sell Germany's mobilization plan to a foreign country. In Germany, this is the first time that anyone has been executed for this crime in peacetime. The Baroness was dressed in ordinary prison clothes and first came to the execution platform. With one stroke of the axe, her head rolled into a blue basket filled with rice crumbs. It is said that Poland's mobilization plan was revealed."

This newspaper (National Telegram from Berlin, March 31): A young woman of twenty-five was sentenced to be beheaded today. Her crime was that she indulged in pleasure in歌臺舞榭 while allowing her three young children to starve to death at home.

This newspaper (Reuters Dispatch from London, April 5): (1) During today's meeting of the House of Commons, Conservative MP Walter House asked about the two German women who were hiding in a house in London and died suddenly yesterday. It was found that one of the two women was Dr. Fabian, a German socialist and writer, and the other was Mrs. Wim, also a writer. It is now believed that both died of free poisoning. Hua asked the authorities to investigate the truth of the matter, as it was heard that the death of the two women was related to foreign political groups.

(2) According to the leader of the Paris Bar Association, Geoffrey, today, it is now known that the sudden death of the two German women hiding in London was not due to suicide. The Germans living in Paris and the Germans who are associated with the two women who died are all uneasy and do not know where to turn for protection. The two women had exposed the activities of the National Socialist Party members in London.

After reading the above news, I know that Germany has sentenced a total of three women to be beheaded in three months. Two women who were hiding in London died suddenly, neither from suicide nor from disease.

Everyone knows that German women have participated in various occupational fronts since the European War, and have gained the right to vote since 1919. They have made considerable achievements in production work and participation in political power. But recently they encountered Hitler, who is good at exploiting them. He used the voting rights of millions of German women as a pillar of the National Socialist Party. Once his dictatorship succeeded, he immediately turned his face and asked them to return to their families, forbidding them from participating in politics and prohibiting them from engaging in paid labor. This is Hitler's exploitation of women and the great reward given to women!

Under this circumstance, German women, instead of obediently staying at home, helping their husbands and raising their children, became spies, spies for the rebels, and of course deserved to die. However, according to the laws of the so-called civilized countries, the punishment of beheading is considered too uncivilized and has been abolished. Hitler's reapplied use is nothing less than the true nature of a tyrant!

The emergence of romantic women has its social roots. Hitler does not carry out fundamental treatment, but only blames one side. The romantic woman may have had other difficulties in letting her three young children starve to death at home while indulging in pleasure in歌臺舞榭. Most middle and lower-class women in Germany are trapped in their livelihoods. Moreover, under the slogan of "giving women's jobs to men," the lives of unemployed women are of course a problem. Therefore, the romantic woman probably wanted to escape from life and seek pleasure. Otherwise, how could her three young children starve to death? However, Hitler does not seek out the root cause that caused them to starve to death, but puts a weak woman to death. The method of putting her to death is also a cruel punishment that civilized countries have not dared to try again—beheading!

As for the news that the two German women died suddenly in London, although the truth is not yet clear, after reading the above news carefully, it is undoubtedly clear that they were coerced to death. Of course, political activities in another country cannot be immediately arrested and beheaded. Therefore, beheading is replaced by causing them to die suddenly. The method cannot be said to be ingenious. Mrs. Ulen said, "The victory of the German National Socialist Party is due to the great efforts of the national women." But what happened to German women after the National Socialist Party won? Let's still use Mrs. Ulen's words to answer: "The current German women have completely eliminated the achievements gained through decades of hard struggle and reversed to the state of the century." (See this magazine's "Women under Hitler's Rule")

German women "have reversed to the state of the Middle Ages." The above news is further proof of this conclusion.

Women's Issues Lecture

Lecture 4: Women in Ancient Slave Society, Section 1: Slave States and the Enslavement of Women 196

Since the decline of the primitive matriarchal system and the establishment of the patriarchal system, many difficult contradictions and oppositions have occurred in ethnic societies. That is to say, there have been many different social strata, such as slaves and slave owners, the rich and the poor, farmers and handicraftsmen, the privileged and the powerless. There are conflicting interests between them, which often cause conflicts and struggles. This struggle not only stirs up social chaos, but even puts the entire society into a crisis of common collapse and death. Therefore, in order to resolve this contradiction, a mediation agency is needed. This agency is the most primitive form of the state. However, with the concentration and strengthening of social economic power, it finally became a power organ used by slave owners or the rich to suppress slaves or the poor. Its oldest and most typical example is the ancient Greek and Roman slave labor system states.

The state also made considerable and effective arrangements in the struggle between matriarchal and patriarchal power. Many social scholars do not pay much attention to this point, but I think this is a question worth studying.

The transition from a matriarchal society to a fundamentally different patriarchal society must have been a major social change, and this change was not implemented so "peacefully." On the contrary, we can see the struggle between patriarchal and matriarchal power in many legends. That is to say, among the warring peoples, there are still many legends about female heroes (Amagon). They led many powerful women soldiers to participate in the war. Even the queen of the African barbarians, the Dagona, is leading an armed female guard. In this way, there is no doubt that men had to go through a long struggle to seize the dominance of women. The state's task in this regard is very important, that is, to stipulate clear laws regarding the issue of men's and women's rights, making women legally in a non-human position. Needless to say, in ancient society, even in the laws of modern civilized countries, the state's organ for suppressing women's rights is fully expressed.

Ancient Greece and Rome built the first brilliant civilization in human history, but this so-called civilization was actually built on the sacrifice of women and the blood and sweat of slaves. It is said that around the fifth century BC, among the 200,000 residents of Athens, Greece, slaves accounted for 100,000, free people only 20,000, and the remaining 80,000 were foreigners without rights. Only these 20,000 free people were a special class with dominance. They absorbed the cream and blood of 100,000 slaves, deprived all women of their human rights, and indulged in extravagance and pleasure. This is the characteristic of the "civilization" of slave society!

Regarding the enslavement of women, Bebel said this: "They were the first humans to become slaves! Before the existence of 'slaves', women were already slaves!" ("Women and Society")

However, there is an essential difference between the enslavement of women and the enslavement of some men. Because firstly, "women" do not belong to the category of social class, it is only an abstract sexual distinction. Therefore, in class society, "women" themselves must also have class divisions. Secondly, the decline in the status of women is based on their loss of the right to important productive labor in the national economy, rather than due to forced labor. This is what we must pay special attention to.

Kolontai said this: "Many people think that the subordination and powerlessness of women are based on the establishment of private property rights, but this is a wrong view... The subordination of women is due to the sexual division of labor, that is, men bear the productive labor, and women bear the auxiliary labor. The more this division of labor is, the more severe the restrictions women suffer... The private property system only helps to promote the subordination of women. (Women's Labor Revolution)

To give an example, in ethnic societies, the status of farming women is still superior to that of pastoral clan women, because farming labor is suitable for women, and women occupy an important position in production. Pastoral labor is suitable for men, and women occupy a supporting position in production. Therefore, although after the collapse of the matriarchal system and the establishment of the private property system, the rights of women continued for a relatively long time among the farming peoples where women occupied an important position in production. However, the private property system gradually split the ethnic community economy into an independent individualistic family economy, and within the family, it also caused the sexual division of labor. In other words, women are responsible for household kitchen work, and men are responsible for productive work outside the home. On the other hand, with the development of economic technology, various occupations other than animal husbandry and agriculture have emerged, thus discovering various specialists, such as potters, leather workers, weavers, merchants, samurai monks, etc. These occupations are all handled by men, and women are only in a supporting position. As a result, women have become unimportant in the national economy. This has also become a household slave for giving birth to children and serving husbands. The status of women in slave society and all male-dominated societies can only be correctly understood from this perspective.

Speaking of the status of women in Greece and Rome, it can no longer be explained with a general concept. Women belonging to free people and women belonging to slaves belong to completely different class categories. The former and the latter have distinctly different lifestyles and identities. However, this difference is only that the former are slaves of free people and the latter are slaves of slaves. The wife or daughter of a free person with dominance naturally has her own things, and it is the remnants of her father's or husband's privileges. They themselves have nothing, and only do work such as washing, weaving, cooking, raising children, and guiding domestic servants in the family. Moreover, they live a long-term life of prostitution under the absolute oppression of men. As for female slaves, their subordinate relationship to male slaves is relatively slow. This is because both men and women are equally powerless, unfree, and subordinate, and suffer the same hardships of labor, distress, fatigue, and hunger. What subordination is there to speak of here! Only the anger and resistance to free people are burning in their hearts.

On Children's Day 197

— Wu

On Children's Day!

Amidst the grand celebrations of Children's Day!

Before the theater doors, silk banners with golden characters on a red background, proclaiming "Celebration Assembly," fluttered in the breeze.

On the walls, posters were plastered, filled with slogans for the welfare of children.

Under the eaves, leaflets more captivating than stories of "Seven Heroes and Five Gallants" were scattered.

Groups of children, led by their teachers, filed through the iron gates of the theater.

Those without teachers—no, the poor children who had never had the fortune to enjoy education—could only clutch the iron gates with small hands, peering inside with longing eyes.

—"Why won't you let me in?"

—"I don't know! Ask the Children's Welfare Association!" The reply was as cold and hard as the ice congealing on the edge of the pond in December!

The "speeches" were always impassioned, and no one would say half a sentence that wasn't fashionable.

However, "Revive the Chinese Nation!" "Defeat Imperialism!"... These were things that the children sitting on the sofas certainly wouldn't understand. Their teachers had only told them, "There will be games to watch!" "There will be gifts to receive!"

Who understands this personal suffering? Those on the coal heaps, in the factories… perhaps right there by the iron gates.

The slogans of the assembly numbered ten in total!

Shouted out, they were truly resounding! As if the theater building itself would collapse.

But, after all, this was a theater, with strong walls and thick doors, completely separating one world from another.

The sounds drifted, drifted… hit the wall! Gone!

Games ahoy!

The children all loved watching the two young ladies with purple and green thin silk headscarves, performing the "Fengyang Flower Drum" dance.

"...Poor families sell their sons, but I have no sons to sell, so I carry my flower drum and travel the land!"

"...How many families are buried in the bellies of fish, how many families have no clothes to wear…"

"...Men died on the battlefield, leaving behind women and mothers in the villages. I have traveled thousands of miles, everywhere there is hunger and cold, everywhere is desolation!"

The singing was even more beautiful than the song of a nightingale!

Hee hee ha ha…

Clap clap clap…

Dismissal!

"Children's Goodie Bags" are here!

—"One for each person, don't rush and grab!" A crowd of children quickly ran over, as those distributing the gifts loudly shouted.

—"Ha! 'Children's Books and Newspapers'! A toothbrush... ha!"

—"Ha! Toothpowder, 'Little Friend'... ha!"

The laughter stretched out long, reaching the iron gates.

The poor children couldn't help but swallow their saliva.

—"Why won't you let me in?" Some anger, some sorrow!

—"I don't know, ask the Children's Welfare Association!" The reply was still cold and hard.

All the same a child!

All the same a "future master"!

All the same a "precious treasure" who lived ten months in their mother's womb before being born!

But...

Open your eyes and look!

German Women Under Hitler 198

— Translated Excerpt from Mrs. Uren's Speech

This article is an excerpt from the speech of Mrs. Uren, a former German Democratic Party protector, delivered on the London Broadcasting Station during the Fourth Current Affairs Conference held in New York on September 27, 1934. The speech fully describes the recent situation of women in Germany. It is specially translated for the reference of those who are interested in women's issues. - Translator

The victory of the German National Socialist Party (Nazi Party) was largely due to German women. In the years before Hitler seized power, the living standards of laborers and the middle class were very low. Therefore, millions of women who had worked for bread were forced to struggle on the front lines of life! Many middle-class women could only settle for the positions of secretaries, clerks, and other low-level jobs. Working women bore the triple burden of being housewives, mothers, and laborers. They all hoped that one day they could avoid this desperate labor for food and clothing. Usually, very few working women could feel the economic and spiritual independence of happiness; most of them regarded work as an unavoidable burden!

Hitler's Deception

Under these circumstances, Hitler happened to put forward the slogan that all men should be given wages sufficient to fully support their families. This was something that German women had been looking forward to day and night. At the same time, he also promised that all young women could be guaranteed to marry and have husbands. Millions of women, burned by this desire, used their voting rights as a pillar of support for the Nazi Party. Therefore, in the electoral districts held separately for men and women, the voter turnout of women was much higher than that of men.

However, by the eighteenth month of the Nazi Party's rule, not only had the great wishes of women not been realized in the slightest, but also the status of women had been transformed into a more unfavorable state! The legal, economic, and political rights of equality between men and women stipulated in the 1918 Constitution were eventually completely abolished!

The Nazi Party vigorously advocated the idea that a wife being a mother is the "natural duty of women." They believed that women's participation in public life and intellectual issues was a result of the decadence of modern life. On February 12, 1934, Bels said at the Nazi Party Women's Congress: "We are making women retreat in all areas of public life. This is not only not a disgrace to women, but it is a restoration of women's honor."

Ignoring Women's Advancement

In fact, the Nazi Party is indifferent to the various achievements made by modern women. They have not seen the good phenomena after women left the kitchen and participated in various intellectual activities. They only see the external changes.

One of the manifestations of this view of women is the great change in women's education. According to the new law, the number of female university students must not exceed one-tenth of the total number of students. Not long ago, various universities in Prussia held a 25th-anniversary celebration of opening universities to women. At this time, German news was written with this headline:

"Today, on the 25th anniversary of women's acquisition of the right to education, women are once again encountering a period of transition that will make them leave the university first."

Restrictions on Women's Education

In Nazi Party schools, girls do not have to receive preparatory education for studying science. The things that women in the new era should study are considered unnecessary.

In a certain periodical, "German Women and Their Tasks," the new elementary education order is described as follows:

"We must understand what kind of knowledge should be taught in today's girls' schools. I think national and family affairs; the science of heredity; the German soul overseas; and knowledge of air defense are all vanguards of the entire line of education. At the same time, swimming, cooking, hiking, family music, and family education are also essential subjects to learn."

In addition, military training has also become an important course for women and children. (To be continued)

Duobaolin in Hankou 199

— Qian

—Price: One Hundred Wen—

Prostitution, like other trades in the society that produces it, has distinctions from top to bottom in goods and prices to suit the status and pockets of its patrons. Moreover, this recognized legal commodity—prostitutes—is like the rice and grain that cannot be missing for a day. Whether it is as noble as princes and marquises or as lowly as dung collectors, it has its supply.

Take Hankou Town as an example. The grades of prostitutes include flower wine costing hundreds or even thousands of yuan, and places where the overnight fee is only one yuan or several dimes. And I also know of a brothel that operates during the day, with each time costing two hundred wen.

Anyone who lives on Central Street, as long as they hear the words "Duobaolin 22," men, regardless of age, will show their yellow teeth and put a smile on their faces that seems contemptuous and greedy. Women, on the other hand, act as if these three words are… as if they haven't heard them, or they slip away. "Duobaolin" is just a small name, and the actual situation in the neighboring alleys is also true. First, at the end of the road, there is a square pond, which is truly a stagnant pond with green water all year round. Not far from the pond is a large public toilet. Third, less than two feet away from the toilet is a well that supplies people with water for washing and drinking. Fourth, and the biggest fact is that in the vicinity to the left and right of that well, there are scattered five or six small, dirty, and dark bungalows. These bungalows are small shops specializing in selling women's bodies.

Because these shops are of a semi-public and semi-private nature, there is no organization. Each family is run by the hostess herself, but the husbands who are the heads of the family can be divided into three categories: one is unemployed vagrants, one is people who cannot make a living due to contracting serious diseases, and one is opium addicts. Moreover, the other three treasures in the four treasures are all factors that contribute to the development and growth of this fourth treasure.

In the stagnant pond of the first treasure, there are several dyeing workshops that bleach cloth all year round. The cloth that is bleached is all blue printed cloth that is sold in the surrounding villages. The meager wages of these bleaching workers are, of course, not enough to support a family in Hankou, where everything is expensive. Therefore, these temporary or permanent single men have unknowingly formed the regular patrons of the five or six small shops.

The benefits of the second treasure, the public toilet, to these five or six houses are even greater than the stagnant pond. Many hawkers whose capital is only about one yuan, clerks in small shops, workers in workshops, or older apprentices—these people are all forced by life to not be able to regularly solve their sexual desires; because most of them cannot afford to marry wives, even if some have married wives in their hometowns, the women are forced to live in the countryside all year round or outside the city where rent and living expenses are cheaper due to their husbands' economic strength. Moreover, the workshops and small shops in the interior still retain the form of the medieval family handicraft era in their treatment of employees. They—the employees and apprentices—except for a few days off during the lunar New Year to go home, are usually forced to live in the master's house, that is, all of their time has been sold to the master. When these poor employees and apprentices go to the public toilet, as long as they have enough copper coins on them, they cannot resist the torment in their hearts, nor can they resist the obvious temptation in front of them, so they often tiptoe into the half-covered board door. People can often see some hawkers selling hot food, selling candy, and selling miscellaneous goods entering the alley after going to the toilet, and in the blink of an eye, both people and burdens disappear behind that board door.

The third treasure, the well, and the first treasure, the water pond, have equally great power over the prosperity of this brothel. The largest consumer of this well is the only large sauce garden in Central Street, ××. Since the well is public, no one will interfere even if the well water is used up in one breath. The owner of the sauce garden understood this point, so although the garden was equipped with tap water, making sauce, making soy sauce, washing melons, washing vegetables, cleaning melons, and pickling vegetables were all done with well water. Whenever the sauce garden started making soy sauce, and when the work of cleaning melons and pickling vegetables started in early autumn, the workers in the backyard of the store, like ants moving house, from dawn to dusk, only saw them carrying well water to the backyard. In a few years, the second concubine of the sauce garden owner had married in. People always said that the well water mixed with urine and feces made him rich. In fact, can well water turn into sauce by itself without manpower? Compared with the boss, the workers in the backyard are really as poor as beggars. The wages of two or three yuan cannot support the wife in the countryside, so their sexual desires are also taken care of by tasting the goods of two hundred wen in the spare time of carrying water.

These semi-private and semi-public prostitutes, because they have a low-profit policy, can also support a family every day with their income on days when the police do not come to cause trouble often. But they, who are trampled under heavy iron hooves and have no other way out, are now the only producers of the family, but if the husband is not happy, he will beat and scold them, and the people around them have always regarded them as natural prostitutes who are not worth mentioning. Even more pitiful is that under this social situation, their women and children are also forced to follow their bloody path to destruction. Among these five or six families, two have daughters. One is named Caiyun, and one is named Qiaoyun. Caiyun's parents are both over thirty years old. When she was thirteen years old, she was sent to the theater to learn opera. Qiaoyun's fate is different. Her father is over fifty, and her mother is only over forty. The two can skip meals every day, but opium cannot be less, so in the year she was fourteen years old, her parents, looking at the money, married her to an old man who was two years older than her father. It is the sixth or seventh concubine, and everyone is still not sure.

Diary of a Concubine 200

— Guan Lu

April 6th

Miss Lian had lunch here today, and after lunch, she sat in my room all the time. Actually, it doesn't seem like Miss Lian comes to our place for any fun. Originally, she didn't need to come often, firstly because of her relationship with the Fifth Concubine, and also because she was raised by our old lady from a young age. It is said that her mother died of postpartum fever after giving birth to her, and later her stepmother didn't love her, so the nanny took her to the countryside to raise her from a young age. She was only brought back by our old lady when she grew up to twelve years old. Later, her stepmother withheld her tuition fees and made her live in school to study. So she often said, "All relationships are about money. If money doesn't make trouble, bad things will happen." Because of her bad experiences from a young age, her body is still not healthy. She said she doesn't blame her stepmother, only her father for being too rich. She is determined not to fight with her stepmother's children for her father's property.

Although Miss Lian is a bit inexplicably opinionated, sometimes the two sentences she says can really hit the heart of the matter. For example, she said today, "A woman's excessive dressing up is entirely for men." I think this is quite right. When I was living a life of hanging up a sign, that kind of life with nine layers of rouge and seven layers of powder every day, almost none of my companions didn't hate it, but in order to do business, to receive guests, even when I was so tired that I didn't want to wash my face, I would rather not wash my face, and the rouge and powder had to be smeared on.

Later, when I was about to get married, I thought that with a fixed husband, this kind of too tedious dressing up could be avoided. Who knew that having a husband was the same, if you didn't want to dress up, the husband would force you to dress up; he said that marrying a wife was like buying something to eat, it had to be palatable and beautiful. Later, I took this sentence to ask many noble ladies, and they said that their husbands all held the same view, but the wording was different. A man spends a lot of money to marry a woman, isn't it for her body and appearance, what else is it for?

April 7th

I'm already six months pregnant with the child in my womb, and I feel tired all day long, but Elder × still asks me to stay up so late with him every day. When we go out, he even forces me to wear high-heeled shoes, I really don't want to walk a step in those kinds of shoes!

Yesterday, I argued with him a few words again because of wearing shoes, and he immediately said, "Now you have shoes to wear, and you still don't wear them, as if you're putting on airs with someone. Look, I won't buy good shoes for you to wear in the future, I'll buy them and send them to Miss Tang!"

Miss Tang, a venereal disease! I already know everything about buying shoes for her, I even know that he's going to marry her, does he still need to use this method to show me at this time!

I really envy Miss Lian, although she dresses plainly and doesn't spend money lavishly, she doesn't rely on other people's money, she is free in everything, her body and everything else belongs to herself. Even if I get married in the future, I will advise her not to rely on her husband, but to do her own thing.

April 20th

These days, I've only been sick, and my belly is getting bigger day by day. Elder × is probably feeling that I'm haggard, and he hasn't even come back for several days in a row. No, it is said that he dislikes me for being old; people all say that women who get close to men too much often age in their youth.

It is men who play with women as if they were fox spirits, and it is also men who throw them away on the dark streets when they have played them out. It is said that Elder × is now going to marry a nineteen-year-old girl.

I think after the child is born, I am determined to go to Hangzhou to find Aunt Jiu, and ask her to introduce me to work in the obstetrics hospital to study nursing, or to go to women's supplementary school, or... In any case, I won't be Elder ×'s wife!

A man is tired of a woman, and her children probably won't be tired of her, the children are also born by him, not brought by the woman. Miss Lian told me to be more optimistic, women with children have nowhere to go; I want to solve this problem with Elder × before I leave, anyway, it's my own child, and I have the right to see it in the future!

April 25th

Mother Chen told me that yesterday Elder × told the old lady to persuade me to go to the hospital to live now. According to Dean Wang yesterday, my body is too bad; due to excessive mental labor, I am now in a state of "hysteria." Furthermore, pregnant women who have had uterine diseases are most afraid of miscarriage or premature birth.

Elder × also said that if I was unwilling to go to the hospital, he would ask the old lady to exaggerate my illness to me, saying that I needed to be isolated from others and have the quietest recuperation.

"Hysteria," an unsound uterus, I don't even know it myself, do I need people to exaggerate it to me so much? I most hope to go to the hospital one day earlier, to leave other people's homes! I even hope for a miscarriage, after a miscarriage, I can get rid of the burden of motherhood. Everyone knows that the most difficult thing for divorced women to live is to have children. Because children do not belong to the country or society, they belong to their parents, and if the feelings of the parents are broken, the children will not be unhappy, and those who care most about the children are mostly not the father, but the mother.

Payment Procedures

The remittance disbursement hours shall be between the 6th and the 10th of the month and between the 16th and 20th of the month, except on Sundays, between the hours of 2 p.m. to 4 p.m. in the afternoon, by the accounting office of this publication. Please bring a slip, which has been marked with the same official seal as the one on the original manuscript when claiming your disbursement. If you intend to draw on previous months as well, you still need to have them separately marked and stamped according to each month, so that it can be affixed to the bottom for record keeping. Regardless of the length of the text or the number of submissions per month, please stamp each submission, so that the seal can be verified when collecting your remuneration. In the event that it is not stamped, it will be treated as an act of declining the reward. Remuneration fees shall only be valid for a six-month period from the date of publication; if there are still any individuals who have yet to collect their disbursements at the end of the term, then you will be regarded as unwilling to receive the reward, and the account shall be cancelled to bring an end to this matter.

We ask that Masters Wanfang, Huanying, and Bo’er please promptly send their official seal, so that they may receive their remuneration fees. Respectfully, from the Shenbao Women's Graphic Editing Room.

Shenbao This City Supplement Amateur Weekly

Amateur Musings

On Independence 202

— Jiang Ren

How can a person construct an interesting and noble life? This is truly a question worthy of people's interest to discuss. Of course, the life we are talking about here is not simply seeking material satisfaction as a complete hedonism, but a kind of enterprising spirit, a manly spirit, and a spirit of perseverance that can be followed by practice. In other words: a person should have a free spirit and an independent personality to make life meaningful.

At any period and in any region, we will never believe that there is no one as intelligent and capable as the great men or scholars who have left a deep impression on us in the past. However, in the end, they still walk on the path of degeneration, or seem to deliberately bring the cradle closer to the tomb, and disappear into the world in an instant, decaying with the grass. Why is it that people of the same opportunity, even people with the same wisdom, have such different distinctions? This is undoubtedly due to the lack of a spirit of advancement, a pure and noble heroic heart, and the characteristics and abilities to preserve the individual. Because a person must have the above three conditions in order to reach the most ideal state of any career or learning. However, to achieve these two conditions, the most important means is to summarize it in independence of thought and behavior.

The water in the sea or ocean, when analyzed, is formed by the collection of small drops. The world, this complex and vast society, is also created by the efforts of individuals. The great reforms in society today, all immortal truths, and various new inventions in the mechanical field, were initially just a plan in an individual's mind, a declaration on the lips, and a novel fantasy. However, later, these plans, declarations, and fantasies, after their multiple efforts and meticulous investigation, succeeded in becoming what is called truth today. This is to clearly tell you that dependence is the most meaningless waste in the world. Only by using your independent spirit to train yourself is the only way out for you to become an outstanding person. At the same time. We can also cite a good example here for comparison. Coleridge was a very strange person with uneven academic brains, but because he lacked the spirit of independence, he was forever trapped in fantasy and planning without practical achievements. I remember Lamb saying in a letter to his friend, "Coleridge is dead now! It is said that he left behind more than 40,000 articles on theology and logic, but none of them were finished." From this, it can be known that no matter how talented he is, if he lacks the courage to move forward independently, failure is still unavoidable.

Although, when it comes to independence, some people will associate it with being considered unrounded and unkind by people in society. Therefore, they think that independence is what madmen say; even if it is not, it must be the behavior of superhumans. So, for the sake of superficial life, they still float up and down with the flow. Obviously, this is a big mistake. Indeed, if the characteristics of an individual tend to be eccentric and cannot be independent in this world, it is naturally a more troublesome thing; however, today it is not necessary to overthink this item, but what should be overthought is that there are too many who are accustomed to being dependent.

Peter Si once said this way: "To be an unusual person, one must first have an independent spirit." Yes, as human beings, we should be like a high mountain standing against the wind, not like a grass that is blown by the wind. In this way, I think our lives will definitely produce infinite meaning from this unique spirit. At the same time, our ordinary lives can also be improved because of this.

Outlying Post Office Agent

Rural Women of the East River 203

— Min

Guangling Correspondence from Guangdong

In rural villages, there are no fashionably dressed modern young ladies, nor are there wives with "sex toys." There are only simple, hardworking, and enduring farm women—the so-called "rural women," which implies labor. However, their labor is not limited to "household chores" (such as washing clothes, cooking, and raising children); they also plant vegetables, weed, harvest beans, and cut wheat... This situation is very common, the same in both the south and north of China. Therefore, the work of rural women is more complicated than that of farmers, and their lives are harder than those of men. However, in many places, women are hampered by the cruel custom of foot-binding, which prevents them from working in the icy fields or undertaking heavy tasks (such as carrying manure, pushing carts, and lifting stones), so they are essentially in an auxiliary position in agricultural work. But this situation is completely different in the East River region of Guangdong.

There, women can be said to be completely liberated physically: no foot-binding, no breast-binding. As a result, they are very strong and do the same work as men. At the same time, they not only perform well in their work, but they can also independently support their families and cope with society—they are good mothers to their children, strong farmers in the fields, and also "brokers" in trade. The saying that "women depend on men for a living" has been shattered by these facts!

This time, I followed the army to eastern Guangdong. The route went through the East River (via Huizhou, Heyuan, Laolong, Wuhua, Meixian, and on to Jiaoling). I passed through many villages and cities. After Huizhou, I saw women carrying loads, including grain and firewood. According to the locals, some were taking their own agricultural products to the market to sell, while others were small vendors specializing in buying and selling. This is a rare sight. Although women in other provinces carry grain to market, they usually only carry it on their backs or in their hands! Also, in markets elsewhere (especially in the north), most of the business is done by men. However, in the East River region, on market days (small markets are called "xu," held every three days), it is all crowded with women.

In this second month of the lunar calendar, it is the season for spring plowing. Along the way, I saw women harrowing the fields. They rolled up their sleeves high, tied their trousers around their thighs, and their healthy arms and smooth legs were naturally exposed. However, they were not trying to seduce men, but for the convenience and agility of their work.

Our troops walked all the way from Huizhou to Jiaoling (a county in eastern Guangdong), and most of the military supplies along the way were carried by women. They could carry at least six boxes of ammunition, each weighing more than ten pounds. They could travel more than sixty li (about 20 miles) a day with such a heavy load and still hurry home when they reached their destination. There are many mountains in the East River region, which makes carrying loads particularly difficult. However, their speed was no slower than that of the army. On level ground, they were simply being held back by our troops. This shows that women who have developed naturally are no more delicate or weak than men.

They carried their loads, mixed in with our "warriors," without any restraint or shyness. They understood that selling labor for food is a legitimate occupation and there is no need to display any pointless shame. So, along the way, there was laughter and talk. When climbing mountains, they sang mountain songs to dispel fatigue. As soon as one person started, everyone would sing in chorus. The singing was not as gentle or melodious as the "Peach Blossom River" sung by modern young ladies, but its strength and passion were exciting. Unfortunately, I was an outsider and could not understand the lyrics!

Their clothes were mostly short (just covering their hips) homespun shirts, with aprons hanging in front to wipe away sweat. They wore a cloth towel on their heads to shield them from the sun and light rain. Their trousers were also very short, and their bare feet were not protected by shoes or socks. In short, their dress was very primitive and simple. Of course, some were more fond of dressing up. Generally speaking, they wore grayish-white foreign cloth shirts, or skirts with embroidered edges, and had three headscarves: red, blue, and white. This dress was by no means fashionable, but on a young girl, it had a unique charm, and the protruding chest and slightly exposed breasts made her look healthier and more lovable.

Their food was also very coarse, almost entirely vegetables. Whenever they carried things for others and had to go more than a few tanglu (ten li is one "tang") away, they would prepare a pack of dry food at home to carry with them. When their stomachs were churning and their bodies were exhausted, they would put down their loads, wipe away their sweat, and swallow the cold food. If it was really hard to swallow, they would take out one or two cents to buy hot water to soak the rice (in Guangdong, a small copper coin is called "one cent," in the East River region it is called "one lei").

This kind of frugality seems excessive to us, but they have no choice! Because the result of selling their labor and sweat every day is, on average, no more than five or six jiao (a dime) of small foreign silver (carrying ammunition is two jiao per tanglu, but this is an exception). This small amount, in addition to maintaining their own necessary living expenses, also has to support their parents who cannot work, or their crying daughters. The heavy burden of the family is on their shoulders, what else can they do but be extra frugal?

Of the women who live this hard life, some still have a small amount of farmland. During the busy farming season, they cultivate their own fields, and when they have free time, they look for opportunities to sell their remaining labor. The rest are mostly hired laborers without land. Besides helping with odd jobs during the busy farming season, their main occupation is carrying goods. However, this occupation is not fixed. Like dockworkers in the city, they only have a livelihood when there is an opportunity to carry goods. So, they take their tools (thick bamboo poles) very early every day and wait on the main roads. When they meet an employer, they crowd around, scrambling for business.

Most of the reason why rural women in the East River region have to independently support their families and make a living is that men go out to do business or go to Nanyang (Southeast Asia) to work (the most overseas Chinese in Nanyang are from the East River and western Fujian). Regardless of whether they do business or work, they are very far away from their families. Many have lost contact altogether and do not take care of their families at all. I have asked many women whose husbands or fathers and brothers have been away from home for more than ten years, or seven or eight years, and they do not know whether they are alive or dead. But they have not given up hope for them, believing that they will eventually earn money and come back!

Overseas Correspondence

Chinese in Europe 204

— Liang Xuewen

Marseille Correspondence from France

Among the Chinese living in Europe, if one were to rank them based on appearance, one could not simply use the same standards as in our homeland. Because a suit and leather shoes are the only marks that distinguish the upper-class Chinese and the middle-class intellectuals in our country, but among the Chinese living in Europe, since wearing a suit and leather shoes is universally the norm, at most one can only distinguish them by how fashionable they are, the quality of the materials, and how clean they are. Although one can usually see Chinese of various shapes and colors wearing work clothes, casual clothes, and formal clothes on the street, on Sundays, most of them wear fairly splendid casual clothes, with a cane hanging on their wrist, and some even have a Western woman in tow, appearing on the streets, streetcars, and in the countryside in the guise of a young gentleman.

The Chinese who reside in Europe, those top-level dignitaries, nobles, and idlers, can only be glimpsed occasionally when they visit some place or at some exhibition. They only appear at banquets, entertainment venues, and conference halls of the upper-class foreign society. So, we do not know what they do or how they live. Students, who are the main component of the Chinese in Europe, both self-funded and government-funded, with the exception of a small number, are either the children of wealthy families with very good financial situations, or they receive subsidies from the national or local government. So, even though they are still studying and do not have a lot of money to spend freely, they still live a more leisurely life than ordinary Chinese. Studying, we dare not deny everything, and some naturally work hard and are self-motivated, but there are also many who specialize in dancing, watching plays, and engaging in social interaction and love with foreign girls.

Merchants, this is a sad story. Like the large Chinese exporters, although they occasionally send resident managers and salesmen to Europe, they are very rare, and even if there are some, they are just a few travelers living in little-known hotels or renting single rooms. If you were to call them Zhuangke (retainers or followers), then putting them in the

Page 20

large industrial and commercial cities of Europe, they are nothing more than brokers of the sixth, seventh, or eighth rank. Chinese merchants who open huge companies, foreign firms, and banks like Europeans do in China, renting or even building multi-story Western-style buildings as business premises, are not even to be seen. If you were to talk about business, then there are at most only three or five Chinese restaurants in major cities such as Marseille, Lyon, Paris, London, and Berlin, which are small like pigeon coops, and most of them only sell food to the Chinese, earning money from their own people to maintain their lives. Those who run these small businesses are Chinese workers who have been in Europe for a long time and have saved a few coins, hard-working students, and students, and are not considered formal merchants.

As for the lower-class Chinese in Europe, the components are more complex, and their origins and the ways they make a living are also uneven. In terms of their origins, most of them are Chinese workers recruited in China by the Allied Powers during the First World War, followed by the work-study students who came to France from 1919 to 1921. Although most of them have returned to China, many have stayed in Europe for a long time, especially in France. Naturally, there are also many who are scattered in Germany, Belgium, and other countries. It is said that the Chinese workers recruited during the Great War were initially under military management in England and France, either being driven to work behind the front lines, or helping them to produce in factories. But no matter where they were, they were housed in barracks specially set up by the War Department, working under military law. After work, they lived in one place, guarded by black soldiers, and could not go out freely. If there was anything unsatisfactory, they would be subject to military punishment. Flogging and imprisonment were common occurrences. In France, they were even taken to Marseille to be imprisoned in water prisons, or sent back to China. Their wages were so low that they could not be lower. In addition to food, they usually only received one-third of the ordinary wage as pocket money. Although the Chinese workers who received this treatment felt pain, they could not escape, because they did not have passports when they came to Europe. If they escaped, all hotels and residences would not dare to accommodate them. Occasionally, if they escaped, they would become blacklisted Chinese workers, and were in danger of being arrested at any time, so they could only sneak around. This situation continued until around 1924 before it improved. Those who did not want to return to China could obtain a residence permit and find work freely. When they were workers, they mostly relied on physical labor for hard work due to their lack of knowledge and lack of technical training. The wages were generally about one-fifth lower than those of workers in the country where they were located. Now, the Chinese workers who have stayed in Europe have some skills, and their living conditions are better than before. Some have also saved a little money by living a subhuman life, but it is not easy to send money back to China, and some have married Western women and started families. Most of them do not want to return to China.

The work-study students originally came to Europe with the grand ambition of studying through work, but this was just their fantasy at the time. After arriving in Europe, they lived a very pitiful life for a period of time during the post-war economic panic and unemployment panic. Some of them died from eating only foreign potatoes and getting bloated diseases, and some were so desperate that they passively committed suicide, but most of them have returned to China. Those who have stayed in Europe now have some skills and have completely become workers. However, because they were intellectuals in China, some of them have a good command of foreign languages, and some have studied and acquired considerable knowledge. Many of those who have stayed in Europe have also married and no longer think about returning to China.

There is also a group of small businessmen who wander around many cities in Europe, selling small trinkets to make a living. The things they sell are just small stone carvings of people, monkeys, cups, bowls, and other toys. Most of these people are from counties such as Qingtian.

Among all these lower-class Chinese, except for the work-study students, many of the components are not pure. For example, among the Chinese workers recruited in the European War, some were soldiers under Zhang Xun, and lost their jobs after his restoration plot failed, and were only recruited to foreign countries. Some had committed murder and robbery and used this opportunity to escape to foreign countries. As for those Chinese who came to Europe without formal recruitment, they were almost all smuggled in. On ships traveling between China and Europe, some were Chinese stewards and stokers, who not only smuggled arms, morphine, and opium, but also smuggled in such vagrants. Anyone who knows this route can come to Europe without a huge fare. If you can find a Chinese steward or stoker, just pay half or one-third of the lowest fare, and if they are their relatives and friends, you may not even have to pay. They will smuggle you into the stoker's cabin at the stern of the ship to sleep, eat with them, and when foreigners come to check, you can hide in the only exposed hole in the stern of the ship where the rudder is, and you can avoid everything. But there are also occasional discoveries, and being discovered is very dangerous. Sometimes the foreign masters will immediately push you into the sea.

Because some of these Chinese are people with extraordinary abilities, some of them also engage in the business of opium and morphine, and even after the war, some lived a life of theft and robbery, committing murder cases. Such Chinese are generally the most despised in Europe, although most Chinese are equally despised. Lower-class Chinese in Europe are simply a kind of yellow slave, no different from black slaves. Their misfortune does not become fortunate just because they have arrived in civilized Europe.

Small Monograph

Critique of Psychoanalysis 205

— Yi Sheng

In 1880, the Viennese doctor Breuer cured a young woman suffering from hysteria by using hypnosis. This matter attracted the attention of the famous Freud, who immediately decided to study with Dr. Breuer, and as a result, the two jointly completed the book "Studies on Hysteria." Later, Freud continued his research and finally completed the famous theoretical system of psychoanalysis.

The psychoanalysis completed by Freud not only showed its brilliance in general psychology and abnormal psychology, but was also applied to history, religion, and art. Generally, Freudians believe that psychoanalysis is omnipotent. In their eyes, all phenomena of human society can only be understood by studying them with the laws of psychoanalysis. Now, Freudianism is not only prevalent in Western Europe, but also has its followers in the relatively backward East Asia, Japan, and China. Kume Masao, in his famous book "Symbolism of Anguish," gave such publicity to psychoanalysis: "This theory (psychoanalysis) has influenced not only psychiatry, but also researchers in pedagogy and social problems. Because Freud also explained the psychology of wit, dreams, legends, and literary creation, there are now many people who apply this theory to literary criticism. Moreover, even strange new terms such as Freudian Romanticism have been heard." From this, it can be seen what an important position psychoanalysis occupies in the general academic world.

Freudianism mainly arises from the special emphasis on human sexual instincts. According to Freud, humans have sexual desires from birth, in infancy. The infant's sucking of milk and the infant's being held in its mother's warm embrace are all satisfying its sexual desires. Because humans have the behavior of loving the opposite sex, in the eyes of Freudians, boys must love their mothers and consider their fathers to be their rivals, and vice versa, daughters prefer their fathers. However, at a certain age, people's sexual desires and all their potential desires are restricted by ethics and morality, and some desires cannot be consciously and clearly expressed. Freud said, "Our unconscious realm is like a huge waiting room, in which various psychological tendencies are crowded together like organisms. This waiting room has a smaller room, like a guest room, connected to it. In this room, the same consciousness exists, but at the entrance from the waiting room to the guest room, there are guards who supervise various mental tendencies, checking them here. If they feel that something is wrong, they will not allow them to enter the guest room. ... Various tendencies are unconscious from the beginning. Because they are blocked by the guard at the entrance and return, they become conscious. At this time, we say that they are being repressed." However, this repressed desire does not disappear because it is repressed. When the conscious review is relaxed, it will revive and turn around, which constitutes bizarre dreams. At the same time, because under conscious review, many of humans' desires in infancy cannot be expressed clearly and directly, they are often excluded and symbolized in imagination. Thus, art, and even religion, history, and many social phenomena are produced. According to Freudians, the sticks and pencils made by humans are symbols of the male reproductive organs, and vases and other objects are symbols of the female reproductive organs. In their eyes, all our words and actions have an inseparable relationship with sexual desires, and even general political movements are only "expressions of the lewd desires of the infant and prehistoric times."

What is the value of such psychoanalysis? We will now give a brief critique of it. Naturally, we do not say, like Schopenhauer, that sexual love does not exist. In reality, sexual love occupies a very important position in life. However, exaggerating the importance of sexual love like Freudians do, saying that all phenomena in the human world have the closest relationship with human sexual desires, is excessive. Take art, for example. Because sexual love occupies a very important position in life, all sculptors, painters, poets, and novelists since ancient times have either taken love stories as the theme of their works, or interspersed some events related to sexual love. In order to increase the persuasive power of their works of art, the forms adopted by artists and the human language and actions used are often related to human sexual love. Sometimes it can even be said that they are issued by the artist's own sexual desires. Therefore, when studying works of art, applying psychoanalysis to analyze the sexual love life expressed by the writer and to analyze the writer's mind is not without help to us. However, humans not only have the instinct to reproduce, but also strive to survive. At the same time, needless to say, reproduction can only be carried out under the premise of being able to survive. Therefore, in the entire life of humans, there is not only sexual love. Social life for survival is the first meaning of life. The meaning of sexual love arises under this first meaning. Art is a reflection of human social life, so we must explain art through human social life. Psychoanalysis, which exaggerates the importance of sexual love, can only help our research, and cannot be used as the only basis for our research on art. Obviously, the sculptures that appeared in the hunting era depict many wild bison and deer that are closely related to human life at that time. If we study them from the perspective of psychoanalysis, what direct relationship do those sculpted wild bison and deer have with human sexual love? In the past feudal agricultural society of China, landscape paintings depicting plants and natural scenery were produced. From the perspective of psychoanalysts, what direct relationship do these landscape paintings have with sexual love? At the same time, even those works of art that take love stories as their theme cannot be understood solely by studying them with psychoanalysis. Because all human words and actions, even their psychology and subconscious, are strictly regulated by their social life, and their psychology and behavior of sexual love cannot be freely developed independently of this regulation. Therefore, the concepts and behaviors of sexual love of people living in various times and societies differ from each other due to their different lives. "For example, in Greece, we have Platonic love, in the Orphic era we have pastoral love, in the era of troubadours we have chivalrous love, in the era of Petrarch and Dante we have mystical love, and in the era of Rousseau, Chateaubriand, and Goethe we have romantic and sentimental love." (Ikowitz) Therefore, if we do not study those works of art that express the concepts and behaviors of love generated by various times and societies from a social perspective, wanting to completely explain them by borrowing psychoanalysis will inevitably be futile, and it is absolutely impossible to understand those works of art.

Literary Works

Decline (End) 206

— Shen Qianli

"Owed rent? When did we owe it?" It was like being hit on the head with a club, a sudden shock that shook me.

"What's the point of saying more? Afu! He just got back, let him rest a bit, okay?"

Looking at my mother's melancholy yet kind face, I felt an indescribable distress in my heart.

"Exactly how much rent do we owe? Is Master Wu so ruthless?" I glared fiercely at Afu.

"How much? I'm not sure, only the old lady knows," Afu said with a bitter face.

"I don't know how Master Wu calculates it either. I remember borrowing only three dan six dou of old rice from him this autumn. When it was being carried over, I even saw a lot of chaff mixed in. But when it came to calculating the money, suddenly it was forty yuan! Just now, Changgen said that your father pleaded with Master Wu for a long time, but he didn't even listen and insisted on forty yuan. I heard that your father is still at Master Wu's house. If he can't figure out a way to pay the rent, things will be bad when they go to the district office!"

"Three dan six dou of rice, for forty yuan?" I really couldn't believe it.

"Borrowing rice in town always involves adding interest," Afu interjected.

"Can't we find any other way to get the money at home?" Although I still had forty-odd yuan with me, thinking about the travel expenses I'd need soon to return to Shanghai, I couldn't help but ask my mother.

"You can't find any foreign money in the countryside these days. This morning, Changgen heard that Master Wu was pressing your father to pay off the rent, so he rushed back to discuss it with me. We took last year's sow and more than ten dan of turnips to town and only got seven yuan in cash. Ugh! A sow weighing over a hundred jin only sold for a little over five yuan. That's not even enough to cover the cost of her feed!" My mother shook her head and sighed.

"Right? We can't even count on having meat for the New Year!" Afu said indignantly.

"Afu! Can we still go to town tonight?"

"What for? Go to town tonight?" My mother asked me urgently.

"Tell Afu to take these forty yuan to pay Master Wu, so we can get Dad back. Isn't it time to 'send off the Kitchen God' tonight?" I took out forty green banknotes from my pocket and placed them on the table in front of my mother.

My mother and Afu, for a moment, were stunned into silence, as if I were a savior who had come to rescue my father.

"Go quickly! Go with Changgen, be careful on the road." Seeing the joy that had yet to recede from the corners of his mouth as he left, I couldn't help but give him some more instructions.

The next morning, I heard my father coughing in the ancestral hall. I hurriedly came out of my room and called out "Dad" but couldn't think of anything else to say.

My father had heard that I was back last night, so he wasn't surprised to see me this morning. He just acknowledged me with a long, drawn-out sound.

A middle-aged man's face was already accumulating wrinkles like those of an old man. The lines at the corners of his mouth were as deep as if cut by a knife, and a line of dry, white beard like a brush hung across his face, as he panted rapidly.

"Is everything settled with Master Wu?" I asked.

He suddenly stopped pacing, glanced at me with worried eyes, and then sluggishly resumed pacing. "What's settled? The forty yuan was given to him? Hmph! They don't care whether it's a drought or a flood, they just want their rent at the appointed time. You can talk until you're dry, but you can't get them to reduce the rent by even a fraction. These people are just too ruthless."

"Forget it, let's plant less this year; we'll just return Master Wu's fields to him."

"Hmph, hmph!" My father looked at me with a cold smile, and then said, "Child, you don't understand this. Master Wu's fields can't be returned. We are born with the fate of oxen, and we're destined to be trampled on. What else can we say this year? We can only hope that the heavens help us, and that the harvest will be good enough to give us a little extra grain. As long as we have a peaceful life, that's good enough. Alas!"

A New Year's Eve slipped away in forced laughter. After living in my hometown for less than a month, after being separated from it for five years, I felt so oppressed by the bleak environment that I no longer wanted to stay.

One morning, amidst the long faces and forced farewells of my family, I said goodbye to my hometown, a place from which I had been estranged for years. Afu carried my luggage ahead, walking quietly. Everyone had a layer of distress buried in their hearts, and no one spoke. After a while, when we arrived at the dock, Afu carried the luggage onto the boat and put it away before coming back down. He stood there on the shore, staring blankly. As the boat was about to leave the dock, I saw a bitter smile plastered on his face.

Amateur Coffee Shop

You Can't Ignore It 207

— Shao Wen

There was a student at a technical school who spent all day and night studying science, hoping to become a top-notch electrical engineer in the future. He didn't care about anything else, not national affairs, not world events. When someone talked about social science theories or practical social problems in front of him, he would find it annoying and want to say that the person was just bragging and had no real skills. In his view, only burying oneself in drawing blueprints was proper work, and only those who understood geometry, algebra, and electrical engineering had real skills; everything else was insignificant. Therefore, he did nothing but work hard at his studies, not even reading the newspaper. As he continued like this, his self-confidence grew day by day, and he absolutely believed that he could learn real skills and become a top-notch electrical engineer. Whenever someone asked him, "Mister, what do you plan to do after you graduate?" he would answer without hesitation, "Of course, become an electrical engineer!"

However, unfortunately, a disaster struck. China, which was doing fine, suddenly experienced a rural economic collapse and industrial and commercial decline. The land in the countryside that was producing money for our aspiring electrical engineer shriveled up. His family's shop in the city also had no buyers and was about to close down. So the old man at home wrote him an airmail letter saying that the family finances were strained and they could no longer support his tuition. After reading this letter, it was as if a huge bomb had exploded on top of his head. His hopes, his courage, and even his life were shattered. All the X, Ys in his head turned into balls of fire, spinning around him. He screamed and shouted, almost going insane!…

From this story, we can see that people living in a real society have an inseparable relationship with all the real social problems; they cannot ignore them. Although the technical school student who wanted to become an electrical engineer ignored the real social problems and only buried himself in studying, the real social problems came to bother him. Clearly, he didn't care about political and economic issues such as rural bankruptcy and industrial and commercial decline, but rural bankruptcy and industrial and commercial decline caused a fundamental problem with his tuition, driving him crazy and turning him into a madman! From this we can say that people living in a real society cannot ignore everything in that real society, no matter what.

If you still don't understand, then feel free to bring up a problem and discuss it with me. You might think that monks have already "seen through the illusions of the world," "entered the empty gate," and absolutely do not "think of the mortal world." That everything in real society has nothing to do with them, so they can ignore everything in real society. But the fact is completely opposite to what you imagine. For example, the monks in the major temples in Shanghai cannot have peace and quiet if they don't network with those gentlemen. Although they don't want to deal with the gentlemen, the gentlemen want to deal with them. More obviously, there are national laws, such as, following continues on the fifth page

Page 21

Page 22

Page 23

laws protecting or confiscating temple property, which they especially cannot ignore. Furthermore, the changes in general social customs also have a great relationship with them. We know how prosperous the temples were in various places and how wealthy the monks were in various places during the flourishing period of Buddhism, but since the Xinhai Revolution, many temples have been turned into schools, and the monks have declined day by day. Although there are still temples and monks in existence now, they are not as prosperous as they used to be. From this, we can see that even monks who have "entered the empty gate" cannot ignore everything in real society. If we move the question from the world of monks to the "world of mortals," it becomes even clearer. Before the January 28th Incident, many compatriots living in Zhabei must have thought that they had no relationship with international politics and therefore did not care about international issues, but when the January 28th Incident broke out, the Japanese cannons destroyed their homes and all their property. Regardless of whether they were willing or not, they had to become refugees. Among the thousands of workers in the Shenxin No. 7 Factory, there may have been some who did not pay much attention to the economic aggression of imperialism against us, but recently the factory was auctioned off by HSBC Bank under the economic aggression of imperialism, and there is an imminent danger of unemployment. The film star Ruan Lingyu, who recently committed suicide, may not have usually cared about social morality, laws, and other issues, and may not have understood the principle of money devouring people, but after a love dispute occurred, she could not ignore it. Morality, law, and all the old forces attacked her together, finally making her unable to survive and committing suicide. Thus, can you still say that people living in a real society can ignore everything in real society? Of course not! Because if you ignore everything in real society, everything in real society will come to bother you, making you unable not to care about everything in real society: this can be illustrated in many of the facts mentioned above.

Because you live in a real society, the economic politics, laws morality, customs and practices of real society all have an inseparable relationship with your life. In fact, you cannot ignore everything in real society, so if you want to have a planned and meaningful life, you must bravely approach reality and understand everything about reality. Because you must understand reality in order to deal with reality in a planned way, otherwise reality will deal with you. Why did the Mister who wanted to become an electrical engineer go crazy after suffering a blow from reality? That is because he held the view of "ignoring everything" (the result of which is that he could not ignore it) and did not approach reality, and therefore did not understand reality. If he had paid close attention to all the real problems in China and understood the real Chinese society, he would not have gone crazy even if he lost his schooling, because understanding reality would have made him know how to deal with reality, and he would never have been dealt with by reality. Why did Ruan Lingyu commit suicide? That is also because she did not understand everything in real society and did not know how to resist the oppression of real society against her, so she was killed by real society. Therefore, we say that no matter what kind of person you are, whether you are in business, working, or editing, if you want to have a planned and meaningful life, and not just muddle through, you must seriously manage reality, understand reality, and thus become the master of reality and deal with reality freely.
