Sunday Literary Society

A Disturbance Caused by a "Literary Salon" 210

— Chu

—A Debate on the Question of "Imitation and Creation"—

Spring, at dusk, in a small "literary salon" (Salons Literaires - "Salon"), a novelist was lying on a sofa smoking a cigarette, leisurely blowing out smoke rings of various sizes. A playwright was standing by the window, playing with his cane, staring blankly into the empty air. There were also two poets sitting in chairs, crossing their legs, reading their newly created poems in low but contented voices. The air in the living room was so quiet. Originally, these writers had gathered here specifically to recite their new works and to praise and criticize each other. But there was also a critic who participated in this "literary salon" who had not yet arrived, so their work could not officially begin immediately. Otherwise, our poets, playwright, and novelist would have long been reciting their masterpieces loudly and with exaggerated movements.

Our poets, playwright, and novelist were originally waiting for the critic to arrive before reciting their masterpieces, but unexpectedly the playwright standing by the window suddenly raised a question to the others. He said: "We often hear those literary theorists say: art is an imitation of life and nature. But some people also say that great works of art are entirely created by the genius or the writer himself. Which of these two is right?"

"Of course, it is the creation of genius!" the two poets answered in unison.

"Ridiculous! Without life and nature, what would a genius writer create?" The novelist stood up, his attitude very impolite.

Thus, the debate on the question officially began.

Poet A—Please don't be impatient! I don't want to talk about what life and nature is with you. I just want to ask you: why are there so many people in the world, but only a few genius poets and genius writers can create great works? Can you say that those works were not created by their unique genius? Also, everyone finds the bright moon lovely, but only a genius poet can describe her loveliness, while ordinary people cannot. Can you deny the great creative power of genius poets?…

Poet B—Take life, for example (he rushed to say before his companion finished), everyone in the world is living, but may I ask how many people understand life? The eyes of great genius writers are particularly sharp, and their emotions are particularly rich, so only they can deeply understand life, and only they can beautifully create life in works of art!

Novelist—You two have probably finished speaking. But, I'm sorry, I don't agree with your theory! It's true that among all human beings, only a few genius writers can create great works of art, but if there were no nature and life, could great geniuses create great works out of thin air? Therefore, great works are not created out of thin air by geniuses, but are the result of their truthfully imitating life and nature. Art is the imitation of life and nature, so the more truthful the writer's imitation of nature and life, the greater the work they create!

Poets A and B—Absurd!…

Playwright—Don't argue (he said as if trying to mediate a dispute). I don't have any preconceived notions. As I see it, you all seem to have reasons. …

At this moment, the doorbell rang. Then the critic walked in.

"Sorry to keep you all waiting!" the newcomer said.

"Don't mention it!… We are now debating a question," the novelist said.

"Ah! What's the matter?"

Then the playwright, who claimed to have no preconceived notions, eagerly told the critic about the situation of their debate just now.

The critic's attitude seemed very calm. After listening to the playwright's words, he thought carefully for a while before saying: "This question is very interesting. I would also like to offer some opinions. …"

Playwright—Good, tell us!

Critic—Yes, I'll first talk about the creation of genius. Indeed, if there were no life, no great genius could create anything out of thin air. ("That's right!"—Novelist) We see that every great work expresses certain social thoughts and emotions. All social poems, social dramas, and social novels naturally describe certain social thoughts and emotions, and even those poems and lyrics that praise the wind and moon are an expression of social consciousness. Li Bai, Meng Haoran, and others' poems that sing the praises of nature all express the thoughts and feelings of a portion of people at that time. If a certain social thought and emotion did not exist in the era and society in which the genius lived, then he could not create that social thought and emotion out of thin air in his work. Goethe was a genius, but he could only write romantic poems and novels in his era, but he could not write new realist works. Li Bai and Du Fu were also geniuses, but they could only write regulated verse in the Tang Dynasty, but they could not write modern-style new poems. Why? Because that kind of thought did not exist in the era and society in which they lived. If thought is formed by human beings in their lives, then the genius writer's description of life can only describe the life that exists in his era and society, and cannot create out of thin air in his work a life that does not exist in his era and society. Therefore, rather than saying that great works are entirely the creation of genius, it is better to say that great works are the product of life and the product of society. …

Poet A—Here comes the sociological viewpoint again!…

Poet B—If great works are the product of society, then there's no use for genius!

Critic—Please don't quarrel, you two! I will also talk about the function of art and the role of writers in society in a while. Now, let me talk about the theory of imitation first. The idea that art is an imitation of life and nature comes from Aristotle, but it is also wrong. ("What?"—Novelist) It's wrong! If art is only an imitation of life and nature, and the more truthfully a work imitates, the greater it is, then the records in courtrooms would be the greatest works of literature, because they truthfully record a kind of human affairs, a kind of human life form. The photographs of people taken by photographers would also be the greatest paintings, because the people in the photos are exactly like the real people they photograph, which can be said to be the most truthful imitation. But no matter what, you can't say that courtroom records are literature, and you can't say that photography is painting! In fact, every writer has a complex brain, with certain thoughts, a certain worldview. His description of life is not an imitation in the manner of a photograph, but a description through his brain and his worldview. Therefore, a writer's creation of works is a description and reflection of social life in his brain. All works of art are artistic reflections of social life, not simple imitations.

Novelist—"Reflection," playing with new terms! Humph, humph! …

Critic—The problem is not something that can be concluded with "humph, humph," we need to argue with theory! … Now I want to talk about the role of writers and their works in society. It is true that great works are the product of society and the artistic reflection of social life, but precisely because works artistically reflect social life, they enable the general reader to know what the reflected social life is like after reading them. If a certain work truthfully reflects social life, then we can understand the truthfulness of social life after reading it, and thus determine our attitude toward life in our cognitive life. In this way, works of art have the function of guiding life and helping life, so although writers and their works are the product of society, they also have a counter-effect on society at the same time. Only in this counter-effect can a genius writer show his greatness.

Poet B—Here comes some kind of sophistry again!

…

The critic hadn't finished speaking, and the two poets and the novelist were very dissatisfied and began to argue with each other. So, in the end, the "literary salon" could only

couldn't be implemented, and from then on, the two poets and the novelist

They went to create their own "salons."

Shenbao Local Supplement Film Special

A Brief History of Film Development (14) 215

— Wen Ying

Sound films created many new stars, but also destroyed many old ones. Emil Jannings, once considered the greatest actor, had to quietly return to Germany due to the popularity of sound films. Although he was born in Brooklyn, New York, his rough voice prevented him from gaining a foothold in the sound film era.

Numerous other film stars also declined due to the popularity of sound films, but there were many inconsistencies. One actress, Bessie Love, had been in the film industry since 1918, making her a veteran. However, she had become a figure of the past several years before sound films became popular. One of the common endings for film actors at that time was to join Broadway vaudeville troupes, so Bessie Love inevitably followed the precedent. But after joining the vaudeville troupe, she learned singing, dancing, and playing the ukulele. It so happened that MGM was about to produce "The Broadway Melody," and Bessie volunteered and became the lead actress in that blockbuster. After the film became popular, Bessie Love's name also rose to prominence.

Bebe Daniels' sudden transformation into a graceful singer was also a miracle in the history of sound films. She had kept her singing voice a secret beforehand, not letting anyone know. But she practiced diligently and worked hard, and on the first night of the film's premiere, even her closest friends were speechless. Conrad Nagel, because of his stage experience, also became a popular choice, and companies competed fiercely for him, even if he had four legs, the companies couldn't outrun each other. Betty Compson had gradually declined after starring in "The Miracle Man" and began making short films. But after sound films became popular, she was soon rediscovered and sought after.

Maurice Chevalier came from France and competed with Lawrence Tibbett for the top spot among singing and dancing stars. Warner obtained John Barrymore and took strict precautions to prevent him from being snatched away by other companies. New York stage stars, enticed by Hollywood's amazing salaries, all boarded the 20th Century Limited train westward. Many succeeded and stayed in the West for a long time. Many returned in disgrace, without even their original positions. They complained to everyone about the evils of Hollywood, but they didn't know that Hollywood itself had no good intentions; it only followed the likes and dislikes of the audience.

The beauty of actresses was no longer the only thing valued as it had been in the past. Actresses who remained popular from the silent film era to the sound film era included Norma Shearer, Greta Garbo, and Joan Crawford. They all took the lead in the trend, quickly catching up and learning to speak their lines. Their determination determined their future. Success is the reward of effort.

Now we have reached the peak of sound films. Looking at recent famous films such as "Little Women," "Imitation of Life," "The Merry Widow," and "It Happened One Night," as well as the currently playing "The Old Maid," how can we find any flaws? Even the endless stream of musical films, although empty and ostentatious, are delicate, magnificent, and complete, with no flaws to be found in the details of the technique. Therefore, we cannot help but feel both surprised and fearful!

What comes after reaching the peak? Decline? That's right, reaching the peak is an end. But the art of film has not yet reached a point where it has an end. We are constantly seeking new and novel things. What will we have in the future? We can no longer discuss this, because this is a story, a history, not a song.

Half craft, half art, but it is acting for people to watch, based on human nature, to win the audience's joy or sorrow. The history of film is the world's most romantic story. (The End)

Film Reviews

Review of "The Mighty Barnum" 216

— Ji Han

The Mighty Barnum

—— Grand Theater ——

Some films are purely for commercial purposes, and we cannot find anything relevant in them. "The Mighty Barnum" is one of these works, and we simply cannot find a theme in it. If we say that it is satirizing businessmen and philistines, then in fact the philistines P.T. Barnum and Bailey here are the ones the audience sympathizes with. Conversely, there is no hint of satire, so what is the motivation for making this film?

Yes, this film may be very good commercially. For example, it not only puts beards on women's faces, children dress up as dwarves, and pretend to be mermaids, but also has tall people and fat women, all of which give people a sense of curiosity, like in a playground, although people also know that those are all fake costumes.

Here, it is just like selling "The Mighty Barnum", relying on the appeal of Wallace Beery and Adolphe Menjou. As for the two of them, they do have likeable personalities here, especially Wallace Beery, who plays Barnum and collects strange people behind his wife's back, which makes the audience laugh constantly. Yes, there are indeed people with such personalities in the world, who try every means to make a fortune, they regard selling "The Mighty Barnum" as a legitimate profession, they change from vagrants to gentlemen, but in front of real gentlemen, they inevitably make all kinds of jokes. However, Barnum is ultimately a person with conscience and emotion. When his wife and daughter leave, his beloved singer also leaves, and his business suffers a disastrous defeat, his pain of loss is indeed a very emotional expression.

However, on the whole, the content of this film is of course empty, and the form is not a particularly successful expression. The screenwriter or director can at most be said to be dutiful. For example, using subtitles to explain the plot is rare in the period of sound film development. Also, Barnum's banquet for guests is a joke, once and again is too much, and after the guests leave, there are still two more times, which simply destroys the atmosphere of sadness. From this, we can see that the director's technique is not very clever, but rather vulgar.

Of course, we are not saying that this film is of no interest. As mentioned earlier, from a business perspective, it is quite likely to be a box office success. As for the later climax, the big fire, and the stampede of wild animals, they are all very tense. But in the midst of the fire, the director allowed Barnum and Bailey, who was sleeping in a coffin, to speak calmly, which is too unreasonable.

The lead actor Wallace Beery, gave people the highest praise for his acting in "Viva Villa!". But in this film, apart from consistently making people laugh, there is no outstanding performance. If people hope to see acting as wonderful as in "Viva Villa!", then it may be difficult to get their wish!

Miscellaneous Notes on "Baboona" 217

— You Jing

"Baboona" — New Light Cinema

Three categories are formed in the popular films: one is made with trained animals, such as "Wild Beasts" and "Dragon Tiger Fight"; one is the "Tarzan" type, with humans and animals performing together; and the third type, like the first half of "Trader Horn" and this "Baboona", is purely based on the activities of animals in the wilderness.

"Baboona" is just like "Trader Horn", without a plot. The front only writes about the departure of the plane, from the dangerous peaks of the snowy Mount Kenya to Africa; then from the life of the soil, the singing and dancing and other scenes? It is explained that it has reached the interior: then it comes into contact with lions, rhinos and elephants and other parts of life, especially the introduction of baboons as an important part of the whole film.

Strictly speaking, this can only be regarded as an adventure news film, and it would be an overestimation to recognize it as a documentary. Because under the cameras of the authors Martin Johnson and his wife, the daily life of baboons and the like, the situation of feeding and educating small animals, and the struggle for survival, such as resisting leopards, are faithfully and relatively detailed. However, this record is not enough for scientific research analysis and system, and the introduction of lions, elephants, rhinos, etc. is also only partial and fragmented.

As for individual pictures, there are quite beautiful shots, and the efforts and loyalty of the authors are also obvious in many vivid and realistic places. But from the overall perspective of the whole film, it lacks Montage techniques too much. Not only are the irrelevant airplane scenes too long and too numerous, but the capture of animal life in general is also too sluggish. As for the slowness of the investigation, it also strengthens the atmosphere and mood of dullness.

Relatively speaking, the photography technology has considerable achievements, and the fact that this film does not tend to be of low taste is also a more commendable advantage.

Miss Yu Ying's First Time on Camera 218

Yu Ying is a newcomer at Tianyi, only sixteen years old this year, very lively and innocent. She is friends with Chen Qixia, and recently officially joined Tianyi. When "Return" was filming on location, it was her turn. It is said that it was her "virgin camera"!

"Human Relations" to be Released Soon 219

Li Pingqian's latest directorial work is "Human Relations," which has been renamed three times. This depicts the story of a coolie's family being scattered and displaced, experiencing all kinds of hardships. The protagonist is played by Gong Jianong, who is famous for his profound and thoughtful acting, and Zheng Xiaoqiu, who is good at playing the sons of wealthy families, along with Zhu Qiuhen, Xu Xinyuan, Xie Yunqing, Yuan Shaomei and others. Li Pingqian has always been particularly careful in allocating actors, so he can make the personalities and living environments of the actors and the characters in the play very consistent. "Human Relations" is particularly successful because of the appropriate allocation of actors. The film has now passed censorship and will be released at the New Light Theater soon.

Star News Flashes 220

(1) Zhou Jianxue and Hu Die have arrived in Leningrad from Moscow.

(2) Following "Daughter Sutra," the second film in which all the directors and all the actors of the Star Film Company collaborated, "National Soul," recently gathered all the actors, and the directors explained the plot in segments.

(3) Xu Lai has recovered from her illness and is now working as usual. "Fallen Flower Season" can be completed in one or two days.

(4) After Jie Qiuxin joined Star, she will play the leading roles in "Big Family" and "National Soul."

(5) "Big Family" and "National Soul" are the concentrated efforts of the Star Film Company, and great attention is paid to the sets, costumes, and furnishings, so the head of the set department, Dong Tianya, personally designed them.

Film Novels

Amateur Reporter (After Office Hours) (3) 221

— Tong Yun

Sherron stared and said, "Mr. Brown, why don't you edit a small newspaper? Then you could publish it, with the first violinist to perform on stage in a swimsuit, what need is there for music criticism?" Jem smiled slyly and said, "Ah, I only now realize that madam is an intellectual." Sherron said, "Regardless of whether I am an intellectual, have you forgotten your own business?" Jem said, "Then I must first ask you, what is your business?" Sherron shrugged her shoulders and said, "Oh... for these few months, first write some high-minded musical commentaries. This newspaper has never published any good commentaries. Then I want to try magazines, or edit one or two myself..."

The certainty in her tone startled Jem Brown, and made him angry. He coughed, raised his voice, and said, "For the sake of madam's even loftier career, I dare not keep you here, first, because I am unwilling for you to waste your precious time on our humble newspaper, and second, to avoid hindering your promising future." Sherron quickly said, "I don't care about any hindrances." Jem said, "But I am too concerned about your future, so I want to do a good deed today. Please go downstairs to see the cashier, and ask him to give you two weeks' salary, and say that you have been fired."

Sherron stood speechless. Her eyes widened, unable to believe that this person had actually fired her. But in a moment, she returned to normal. She stood up and said, "According to your ability to appreciate music, one day you will publish a photo of a swimming woman next to a large loudspeaker in your newspaper. Isn't that what your readers like to see?" Jem listened, but wasn't angry, and just nodded repeatedly, saying, "This business is really good. When you see the cashier, ask him to give you an additional five dollars as a bonus. This idea is too wonderful. Goodbye..." Sherron also said, "Goodbye," and walked out in a disgruntled manner.

That night was the first night of the "Double Gems of the Opera World" opening. James Brown was also among the crowd, but he didn't arrive until the second intermission. He had never watched a play from beginning to end, but he didn't care, because his intention was not really about the play itself. At this time, ladies and young ladies were wearing revealing, gorgeous evening gowns, and gentlemen were wearing dinner suits. During the intermission, everyone was mingling in the lobby. James stood in the crowd, thinking that in such a place, where so many people gathered together, there must be excellent news material, if only someone could find it.

Sure enough, before he could finish the thought, he had already seen four people walking side by side across from him. Patterson and his wife, Pennester, and Sharon Nagato. When he saw them, he involuntarily walked over. He was no longer a playgoer, but an active news reporter. He remembered that he had sworn to find out the truth about the Patterson case, so he dared not be negligent.

He greeted the banking magnate and his wife. His eyes couldn't help but glance repeatedly at the handsome man next to them, whose hair was combed so smoothly that flies couldn't land on it. He said, "Ha, Pennester, the last time I saw you was during the rowing race." He then turned to Sherron and said, "Miss Nagato, long time no see, since..." He grinned. Sherron continued, "Since this morning, when you fired me." He raised his head high, leaned on Pennester, and asked him for a cigarette. (To be continued)
